<div id="review_1196550337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1196550337" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1196550337?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8987161-the-duff">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=pea-favorites">pea-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=being-made-into-movie">being-made-into-movie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1196550337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9441244961277724501"><br/>**Re-read: TOTALLY LIFTED MY MOOD AND GOT ME THROUGH THIS HORRIBLE WEEK. I adore you Wesley Rush!!!! ♥<br/><br/><b><i>I was in the middle of asking myself the age-old question-</i>where will I use this in real life?<i>-when I felt a hand on my shoulder. That skin-crawly thing happened, and I knew exactly who was behind me.<br/>Great. Just fucking great.</i></b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/lucy-hale-omg_zpstz5iv9wv.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427463923ra/14272712.gif' alt=' photo lucy-hale-omg_zpstz5iv9wv.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Aaaahhhh this book. This book made me so unbelievably happy, it's unreal. I was completely and utterly obsessed from the minute I picked it up until the moment I put it </span>
  <span id="freeText9441244961277724501" style="display:none"><br>**Re-read: TOTALLY LIFTED MY MOOD AND GOT ME THROUGH THIS HORRIBLE WEEK. I adore you Wesley Rush!!!! ♥<br><br><b><i>I was in the middle of asking myself the age-old question-</i>where will I use this in real life?<i>-when I felt a hand on my shoulder. That skin-crawly thing happened, and I knew exactly who was behind me.<br>Great. Just fucking great.</i></b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/lucy-hale-omg_zpstz5iv9wv.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427463923ra/14272712.gif" alt=" photo lucy-hale-omg_zpstz5iv9wv.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Aaaahhhh this book. This book made me so unbelievably happy, it's unreal. I was completely and utterly obsessed from the minute I picked it up until the moment I put it down. I grumbled when I had to go to sleep and I tossed and turned for what felt like an eternity, struggling internally to keep my head on the pillow and not roll over to pick my Ipad up again. It's not that it was deep or heartfelt or altogether meaningful, I suppose, but <b>the author created this wonderfully cliched world that I felt myself instantly addicted and drawn to, and these characters embedded themselves deep into my heart where I didn't ever want to let them go.</b> It didn't need to be anything other than what it was-fun. <br><br><b>"Hey, you never told me why you were upset the other night," he said. "You were too busy shoving your tongue down my throat. So what was the problem?"<br>"None of your-," I began, but I stopped suddenly. "Hey! I didn't...there was no tongue!" A shiver of rage ran through me as I noticed his mischievous smile. "You son of a bitch! Get the fuck out of here. God, why are you stalking me? I thought Wesley Rush didn't chase girls. I thought they chased him, right?"</b> <br><br>I'm not going to lie-I was ready for a DNF. I know, I know, total case of judging the book by it's horrendous cover, but come on, Guys-look at it! Sad. Anyway. I saw the mixed reviews, I heard the movie was better, I found it was full of cliches, and...er....yeah, this is awkward-<b>I heard the author was seventeen when she wrote this.</b> All negative, if you ask me. I know, I'm a total bitch, right? But there were so many alarming red flags that had me so nervous when I picked this one up. And, I'll admit it, I totally had my nose turned up like a snooty Who from Whoville when I began reading. I was all 'Hmm. That happened quickly' and 'Oh, well she's a bitch' or 'Hmm. I don't like that they hang out here.' But oh mah gah was I proven wrong. Each page that passed I felt myself sinking deeper and deeper until I eventually was so wrapped around this book's pretty little finger that I couldn't see straight. And you know what?? <b>It's never felt so good to be wrong.</b><br><br><b>I was fully conscious of Wesley's hand as it slid up my torso and moved to cup my breast. With an effort, I pushed him away from me. His eyes were wide as he leaned back. "Please don't slap me again," he said.<br>"Shut up."</b><br><br>Oh, Bianca, you bitchy little not-so-Duff. The inner workings of her mind were so funny, albeit very opinionated. She definitely had a venomous bite, but I never felt put off by her harsh judgements or crude rationalizations. Her reasons to start hanging with Wesley were wrong from the beginning, but she never once forgot that fact. Hiding it from her friends, attempting to escape reality, and scrutenizing others that were basically doing the same thing as her, she was in no position to judge...yet she did, repeatedly. And that's where I think a lot of people might have had a problem with her-but I didn't. I dunno. I thought that was kind of realistic. I pull a 'pot calling the kettle black' frequently when it concerns myself and other people, no matter how nice I am or how much I like people-it's human nature to be a wee bit judgemental, and I can't say I'm not...'cuz I am. No, I think my only problem with this whole story was how she continually put herself down. She repeatedly called herself the Duff and questioned why anyone liked her, why Wesley would possibly waste his time with her. It was a very noticeable thing throughout the story, but thankfully I loved her and Wesley so much it just didn't matter-but I can see how this could possibly annoy others.<br><br><b>I jerked out from under Wesley's hand and spun to face him, gripping my pencil like a dart and aiming it right at his Adam's apple.<br>He didn't even flinch. His gray eyes examined the pencil with feigned curiosity and he said, "Interesting. Is this how you greet all the boys you like?"<br>"I <i>don't</i> like you."<br>"Does that mean you love me, then?"</b><br><br>And WESLEY!!! EEPS!! <b>I Can. Not. Believe. How much I loved him.</b> He was cocky. He was arrogant. He was quirky. He was sexy. He gave me butterflies that I continually choked on...Okay. Fuck. I TOTALLY get why I loved him. But that's besides the point!! From the moment we meet him *cough* page two *cough* I was raising my eyebrow sardonically (Okay, in my head I was. I'd had a couple glasses of wine....but that's neither here nor there). I mean, we meet him THAT early?? Gag. I hate when that happens. But OMG, my fears were squelched when he not so subtlety inserted himself in her life every single day. They formed this adorable bond that made them secret friends, then secret *bleep* buddies, and then....something more?? I found myself laughing out loud so much when he was around that my smile became permanent. My heart broke the more we found out about him. My heart soared when he defended her. And my smile was depraved when he got jealous. But, mostly, <b>there were butterflies.</b> Endless butterflies.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_msay6qUuzM1scoxapo1_500_zpspzqpepob.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427465629ra/14272889.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_msay6qUuzM1scoxapo1_500_zpspzqpepob.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book, to me, was unputdownable. I read it at work. I thought about it when I wasn't reading it. I lost many hours of sleep over it. And I stayed up until almost one on a work night without even realizing it until I looked up and saw what programming was on tv-randomly, I might add. So, to say I didn't love this would be false. I adored it. I cherished it. I'm guna go buy the movie version book for my bookshelf (I'm sorry, I can't do that fugly cover. Just...No.). I, my friends, am still obsessed. I cannot wait until I can read it again.<br><br><b>Cute, funny, heart-warming, and addicting beyond all measure.</b> This young author wrote my dream book for this moment in my life-I will never be so judgemental again (Lies. All lies. But, that would circle the point I'm trying to make-oops) before I really know what I'm talking about. I won't judge a book by it's cover. And I will try not to be biased. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/WOkaw_zps0amuhonc.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427465527i/14272877.png" alt=" photo WOkaw_zps0amuhonc.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oops. Just like Bianca. Guess I'll never learn my lesson *shrugs* but I'm so glad I broke my completely rigid mold of rules for this one. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>No matter where you go or what you do to distract yourself, reality catches up with you eventually.</i>
</b><br><br><br><br><br>For more of my reviews, please visit:<br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_104213815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104213815" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104213815?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316084246" href="/book/show/9662548-the-duff">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=given-away">given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer104213815&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104213815" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12118515954412496130">So. I finished <b>The DUFF</b> yesterday and I’ve calmed down a little after being majorly annoyed with its main character, Bianca. Sorry, but how can a supposedly intelligent person be so dumb and so clueless? The only explanation I can think of: Someone gave her very bad advice.<br/><br/><i>“Hey, my father is a dry alcoholic, hasn’t been drinking for almost 18 years, and now consumes huge amounts of beer and whiskey because my mom left him.”</i> - Better not tell anyone, it is his secret and you’re not in the positio</span>
  <span id="freeText12118515954412496130" style="display:none">So. I finished <b>The DUFF</b> yesterday and I’ve calmed down a little after being majorly annoyed with its main character, Bianca. Sorry, but how can a supposedly intelligent person be so dumb and so clueless? The only explanation I can think of: Someone gave her very bad advice.<br /><br /><i>“Hey, my father is a dry alcoholic, hasn’t been drinking for almost 18 years, and now consumes huge amounts of beer and whiskey because my mom left him.”</i> - Better not tell anyone, it is his secret and you’re not in the position to reveal it. It’s just a phase anyway, it’ll pass.<br /><br /><i>“My mom has been neglecting our family for years. She’s always travelling and rarely stays at home with us anymore. Now she sent the divorce papers and my father is devastated. I’m really angry at my mother. Why couldn’t she come home to talk to him at least?”</i> - Don’t be angry at your mother, she just does what’s best for her and your father. You should totally change your opinion about her behaviour the second you see her again and support all her decisions. It doesn’t matter that she’s the reason your father is drinking again and there is no reason to be angry at all – not even a little.<br /><br /><i>“I’m sleeping with this super hot, but also arrogant guy I pretend to hate to distract myself from my problems. When he touches me, I feel dirty afterwards, but it also makes me feel so much better. Is that normal?”</i> - It is a perfectly normal thing that something that makes you feel dirty also makes you feel better. Not weird at all.<br /> <br /><i>“I thought about the other thing again: My father really is drinking a lot and last night, he hit me and called me a whore. A friend rescued me and I spent the night at his house. Are you sure I shouldn’t do anything?”</i> - Just forget about it the moment you leave the house. Your father will come to his senses, go to AA meetings from now on, never drink again and everything will be alright between the two of you. <br /><br /><i>“Another thing: I am also neglecting my friends over this guy I mentioned before. I don’t want to tell them what’s going on. Actually, my best friend is already suspicious and angry at me for not talking to her anymore.”</i> - Just do nothing and carefully avoid her. It doesn’t matter if she is pissed after she finds out – which is inevitable. <br /><br /><i>“I think I have feelings for this guy I’m seeing, although I know it’s pointless because he’s not interested in relationships. But there also is this very nice boy that’s interested in me. I’ve had a crush on him before the thing with Wesley and now is my chance. Maybe I should date him instead?”</i> - Definitely. Go out with the nice boy, he’s a much better choice and you should just ignore the feelings you have for the other guy. He’d only hurt you anyway. Also, a book without a love triangle is a bad book. There have to be two guys in your life.<br /><br />Obviously, this review is to be taken with a grain of salt. I was really looking forward to reading <b>The DUFF</b>, because in a way, it sounded similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1754206.Perfect_You" title="Perfect You by Elizabeth Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect You</a> - which I loved. Therefore, I was really disappointed at the outcome. I think this is one of those books you either hate or love. I have not managed to find any indications on what makes you love it or hate it, though. But I think if you can sympathize with Bianca this could turn out to be a great read for you.<br />Well, as you might have deducted from my review and rating, I’m more on the hate side (although “hate” is definitely too strong of an expression). The main character annoyed me, and despite the sexy premise, I didn’t feel any chemistry between Bianca and Wesley. <br /><br />I’d say: If you want to read this book, give it a try and see for yourself if it is for you or not. It is really hard to give a recommendation here because it is almost impossible to draw the line - when will a character annoy you and when will you like him despite his faults.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12118515954412496130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_972757751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972757751" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1166756280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1166756280" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1166756280?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1166756280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2683894472615168558"><b> 4.5 Duffy stars!!! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “No matter where you go or what you do to distract yourself, reality catches up with you eventually.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/theduff.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421173556i/13334031.png' alt=' photo theduff.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>OMIGOSH YOU GUYS! I loved this book!! Like seriously, I kind of can't believe how much I loved a book that literally means "ugly fat friend".<br/><br/>Over the years I've seen this book in passing, in the library, bookstores, and lists titled "Best Book Boyfriends". I never picked it up because come on. Look at the title. Now look at the cover. Based on those two things, would y</span>
  <span id="freeText2683894472615168558" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Duffy stars!!! </b><br><br><b> <i> “No matter where you go or what you do to distract yourself, reality catches up with you eventually.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/theduff.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421173556i/13334031.png" alt=" photo theduff.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>OMIGOSH YOU GUYS! I loved this book!! Like seriously, I kind of can't believe how much I loved a book that literally means "ugly fat friend".<br><br>Over the years I've seen this book in passing, in the library, bookstores, and lists titled "Best Book Boyfriends". I never picked it up because come on. Look at the title. Now look at the cover. Based on those two things, would you read it? Well this is an extreme case of don't judge a book by its cover... or its title.<br><br>Bianca is a cynical girl, but her friends don't mind it. They love her for who she is. One night when all three are out, Bianca finds herself near the school manwhore Wesley, who proceeds to educate her on the fact that she is the Duff. Designated Ugly Fat Friend. This title makes Bianca's head spin, and she goes into a small identity crisis. On top of that, things aren't so good with her parents and her life around her is falling apart. Assigned to work on a project together, Bianca and Wesley end up having a secret friends with benefits relationship, both trying to escape their crappy real lives.<br><br>As I stated before, I loved this book. Because <b> it surprised me. </b> Bianca was a character I loved so much. She was ridiculously cynical, and I guess maybe I am too because most of the time when she would say something, I'd be sitting there nodding my head and going "hey, I would say that!"<br><br>And this book had some seriously funny moments and dialogue in it. For example:<br><br><b> <i> “Spanish, huh?" he said, glancing down at the scattered papers as he grabbed them. "Can you say anything interesting?"<br>"El tono de tu voz hace que queria estrangularme." I stood up and waited for him to hand over my papers.<br>"That sounds sexy," he said, getting to his feet and handing me the stack of Spanish work he'd swept together. "What's it mean?"<br>"The sound of your voice makes me want to strangle myself."<br>"Kinky.”<br><br>“Your sense of humor needs some work, then," Wesley suggested. "Most girls find my jokes charming."<br>"Those girls must have IQs low enough to trip over.”<br><br>“I mean, there is a reason its initials are VD. I bet you more people contract syphilis on Valentine's Day than on any other day of the year. What a cause for celebration.”<br><br>"Vagina, vagina, vagina. Get over it, Jess. You have one. You can call it what it is." </i> </b><br><br>Despite having a sense of humor, this book also dealt with serious teen issues. Bianca's parents were going through a divorce and her dad was becoming less and less present, and she didn't know how to deal with it. Bianca's former asshole of an ex-boyfriend shows up in town with his new fiance. Wesley's parents are always gone and his crone of a grandmother won't let him see his sister. Lots of teen drama rama.<br><br>The other things that surprised me about this book? There was so much sex! Like from the beginning. Would you look at this hot pink and yellow cover and think you were in for a large round of young adult fade to black? Not me! It was kind of refreshing to read a teen book and have it be realistic about what teens are experiencing in real life. <br><br>And Wesley. *sigh* I loved that asshole. Like, he was such a freaking jerk in the beginning, but like Bianca, the more I saw him in the book I couldn't help but swoon over his arrogant ass. I agree with the list, he's a great book boyfriend.<br><br><b> <i> “Don’t lie to yourself because you think it’s safer. Reality doesn’t work like that." </i> </b><br><br>At the end of the day, everyone who reads this review is going to read whatever the heck they want. I'm the same way. But, I encourage you to ignore the title and cover, and to read this gem of a book. That or go and see the movie when it comes out this February. Hopefully it doesn't suck.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2683894472615168558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Well, when known manwhore, Wesley informs Bianca that she is in fact the Duff of her group, she is left spinning.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421274369i/13351864.jpg" width="400" height="228" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This revelation comes at the same time Bianca's home life is taking a nosedive.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer794778009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15838584718871493063">This book. WOW. Another soul-mate book. I decided to read it because of the movie trailer,BUT its NOTHING like the trailer. This book is deep and thought provoking. <br/><br/>Bianca, the DUFF, is not your regular 'misfit' or protagonist. She's cynic,smart,protective,loving. And her friends though they are pretty, are not dumb blondes as the trailer suggests. They are pretty amazing people. Casey and Jessica are two brilliant friends. Wesley is NOT how he's presented in the trailer either. In book,he has d</span>
  <span id="freeText15838584718871493063" style="display:none">This book. WOW. Another soul-mate book. I decided to read it because of the movie trailer,BUT its NOTHING like the trailer. This book is deep and thought provoking. <br /><br />Bianca, the DUFF, is not your regular 'misfit' or protagonist. She's cynic,smart,protective,loving. And her friends though they are pretty, are not dumb blondes as the trailer suggests. They are pretty amazing people. Casey and Jessica are two brilliant friends. Wesley is NOT how he's presented in the trailer either. In book,he has depth,a background that made him the way he is. and he never tried to FIX Bianca. or have a make over or whatever. Actually noone did. In this book NOONE has a make-over. Shocking,i know. <br /><br />Wesley and Bianca are OTP. and this book is so special. not just because i can relate sometimes with Bianca,but because sometimes i can't. This book does not fit any line or category. Its not predictable. It keeps you guessing. The ending made me think a few things over in my life. and THAT is what makes a great book in my opinion. Its the kind of book that changes you. Its good. Rainbow Rowell book,good.<br /><br />PS: In the movie trailer,i noticed a lack of curls in Wesley's head. WHY? Where are the curls? I demand black curls!!! </span>

<div id="review_1199423765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1199423765" />
    <a title="Simone Elkeles" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39719470-simone-elkeles"><img alt="Simone Elkeles" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442462908p2/39719470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1199423765?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2015</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16345671268372038301">I am so glad that this book is now a movie - it was a cute, fun, sexy read (edgy - so it's for older teens) and I loved it. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1225411019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225411019" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225411019?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carmen by: </span>
      Lots of people
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225411019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15541297649915492984"><i>Now he was the one who looked angry.<br/><br/>Angry and HURT.<br/><br/>I didn't get it.</i><br/><br/>Okay. People will tell you all sorts of things about this novel. But you come here to hear the truth, right? And the truth is that what this novel is REALLY about is a girl who is one of the stupidest characters ever created. Someone who just does not grasp human relationships and interactions. She's an idiot.<br/><br/>Did you ever see 10 THINGS I HATE ABOUT YOU? Yeah? Bianca, the MC in this novel, is like Julia Stiles was in that movie. (</span>
  <span id="freeText15541297649915492984" style="display:none"><i>Now he was the one who looked angry.<br /><br />Angry and HURT.<br /><br />I didn't get it.</i><br /><br />Okay. People will tell you all sorts of things about this novel. But you come here to hear the truth, right? And the truth is that what this novel is REALLY about is a girl who is one of the stupidest characters ever created. Someone who just does not grasp human relationships and interactions. She's an idiot.<br /><br />Did you ever see 10 THINGS I HATE ABOUT YOU? Yeah? Bianca, the MC in this novel, is like Julia Stiles was in that movie. (Except brainless.) Bitter, cynical, and lashing out an anyone and everyone she can. Mainly because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she lost her virginity to her best friend's older brother when she was 14. Their relationship was a total secret. But she didn't know it was a secret because he really had a serious, long-term girlfriend. Bianca was "the other woman" and she didn't even notice. No wonder he never took her on dates and was so secretive about her. Also, did I mention he was 18 and she was 14? Yeah. They date for 3 months before his girlfriend corners Bianca and tells her to back off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Because of this traumatic experience, Bianca is one of those people who hates school dances, hates Valentine's Day, doesn't "believe" in love, etc. etc. etc. But her two sweet, beautiful best friends (Casey and Jessica) adore her anyway. <br /><br />One night, while at the non-alcohol, under-21 club that her friends insist on dragging her to all the time, a hot guy in her class named Wesley approaches her. He informs her that her two best friends are gorgeous, and that he is winning points by being seen talking to her, the DUFF. When she asks him what that is, he tells her that it means Designated Ugly Fat Friend. She promptly spills her Cherry Coke all over his head.<br /><br />But in case you think that this is a little girly teenage novel with problems that consist of this kind of thing, you quickly are corrected. Bianca's mom hasn't been home in a long time. And her dad is fighting frequently with her on the phone. Her father, who has been sober for 18 years, is having a hard time dealing with the fact that his wife might never be coming home.<br /><br />Bianca has a hard time coping with this drama. Not to mention the fact that she finds out her evil ex is coming back into town. She needs something to dull her pain and empty her mind. Something male...<br />...<br /><br />This book was completely confusing to me. For one thing, Bianca is a complete moron who had me seriously wonder if she had been dropped on her head as an infant. Here are some newsflashes for you:<br /><br />If you ignore your friends, refuse to see them, and won't take their calls... they might be a little angry with you and think you don't like them anymore. Sounds obvious, right? Not to Bianca.<br /><br />If you are having sex on the regular with a man, let's say 3-4 times a week, and are spending a lot of time with him, and then suddenly break it off for no apparent reason, he might be hurt and worried. Sounds obvious, right? Not to Bianca.<br /><br />If every time a man sees you, he has a huge erection, tries to get you naked, and fucks you into next Saturday... then he's attracted to you. SAY WHAT? No, really, it's true. Those are signs that a man might actually think you are sexy. I know. It's a crazy concept. Certainly Bianca doesn't understand it.<br /><br /><br />Now you know the levels of stupidity I'm dealing with.<br /><br />There are other things that confused me. For one thing, it's often talked about malicious cheerleaders who keep ugly or shy freshman girls as "pets," basically ordering them to do menial tasks and verbally abusing them. I have never seen this in real life. Were the cheerleaders pretty? Yes. Were they more 'popular' than other students? Yes. Were they ever total verbally abusive jerks to some poor underclassman girl who was sad and lonely? Um, NO. Emphatically not. Actually, in my experience, the popular kids didn't really pay much attention to anyone not in their crowd. I'm baffled by this prevalent media portrayal of evil, abusive cheerleaders who make other kids' lives hell. One, you can easily get kicked off the squad for that shit. Two, part of being popular is at least PRETENDING to be friendly to everyone, even if you didn't give a care. So... that part is a fail.<br /><br />Keplinger seems to embrace caricatures and stereotypes. The jocks, the cheerleaders, the debate team, the band geeks, whatever insert stereotype here. I never really found high school to be divided up that easily.<br /><br />ANOTHER THING<br />Apparently, everyone is having sex. And is super-confident about having sex. I'm pretty sure that even in 2015, the majority of high schoolers have either a.) pretty tame or b.) nonexistent sex lives. College is a different story, but high school? It was pretty rare to even have two or three sexual partners in high school, much less the 50 or so we're supposed to believe Wesley is pulling. In high school? Are you kidding me? You live with your parents and a lot of people don't even have their own car.<br /><br />And have you ever seen or talked to high school kids? High school boys? They are far from the swaggering, confident, sexually powerful teens in this book. Most ADULTS can't even handle meaningless sex - much less teenagers who haven't even been exposed to the world yet. And most adults don't possess the sexual confidence and absolute surety that Wesley possesses. He never doubts himself, seems awkward, second-guesses himself, needs reassurance in bed, or expresses any kind of weakness of any kind.<br /><br />Which is complete bullshit.<br /><br />YET ANOTHER THING<br />You'd think, after all the bullshit Bianca went through with her ex, that the last thing on Earth she'd want is another secretive, no-one-can-know relationship. Yet that's exactly what she goes for and embraces wholeheartedly. It didn't make any sense to me.<br /><br /><i>Pretending</i> you don't have any emotions is one thing. Actually being a soulless potato? That's quite another. And it's very obvious throughout the book that Bianca has no idea what constitutes a friend, a boyfriend, love, friendship or even simple human kindness and decency. This would be much easier to take if she was supposed to be psychologically abnormal in some way. But I think she's supposed to be a neurotypical, non-disorder/sociopathic/psychopathic/whatever teen. Which was a fail. I found myself wondering how this girl had made any friends at all.<br /><br />MESSAGE<br />This book has a message, and it's a positive one, basically saying that everyone gets lumped with stereotypes that serve to box them in and hurt them. I didn't think the message was cheesy or overdone. I rather liked it.<br /><br />HYPOCRITE<br />Bianca's a hypocrite. But she knows that and occasionally admits that, so all the slut/whore/tramp stuff didn't bother me as much as it usually does. Bianca is self-aware and it's obvious that Keplinger is trying to slowly teach her a lesson. It's very sad that girls internalize this slut/whore label, but I didn't feel it was unrealistic and I also felt that Keplinger's end message was against this. If you expect me to go on a feminist rant here, it's not going to happen. Please see my other reviews, there are tons of feminist rants there. ;)<br /><br />ALCOHOLISM<br />After having just finished reading King's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining___1_" title="The Shining (The Shining, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a>, it was startling to once again be plunged into a story with an alcoholic abusive father with a bad temper. The one scene where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bianca's dad calls her a whore over and over and strikes her in the face <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was really tough for me to read. And it was even MORE frustrating that Bianca's dad's alcoholism is completely tied up in a neat little bow, never to be heard from again by the end of the novel. Um, that's a total lie. Getting knocked off the wagon after 18 years is a big fucking deal. Not just some tiny, pesky, easily solved, insignificant problem. I was hoping Keplinger would at least hint at this, but no. Sunshine and flowers all the way in YA, man. Not to mention having your father <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[hit you for the first time ever and call you a whore repeatedly <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> would have much more lasting and significant psychological damage than is presented here. Instead, it's like, "Oh, don't worry about it, Dad! Best friends again? Yay!"<br /><br />And like father like daughter: Bianca is using sex with Wesley to go blotto and erase her worries just like her Daddy is using alcohol to go blotto and erase his worries.<br /><br />SEX<br />I was happy and relieved that this novel portrays teenagers have safe, protected sex. And at no point does it try to pretend that teenagers aren't a.) having or b.) trying to have sex. This is much healthier than crap "celibate" YA where people just kiss, or something. But, let me tell you about some complete and utter bullshit. At the end, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Bianca informs Wesley that they will no longer be having sex. That they will have to slowly work up to having sex again. Why? Because Vicki, a girl at school, had a pregnancy scare. This is horrible. I completely believe in moving slow towards having sex. I completely believe in slowly getting to know a person before you let them go to bed with you. At the beginning of the relationship, take things slow and never let someone pressure you into doing something sexually you are not comfortable with. It could take months for sex to happen. A year. More. Especially for a virgin in high school.<br /><br />But let's be honest, Bianca and Wesley are WAY BEYOND THAT here. They have been having sex steadily for about 3 months now. I estimate about 65 times. You can't have sex with a man 65 times and then just tell him he's cut off for no good reason - oh, but you're still dating and you're still an exclusive couple. That's really cruel. I don't like it. ALSO, as a teenager Bianca probably doesn't know this, but being with a guy who is as amazing and attentive in bed as Wesley is is NOT something that comes around every day. She should be having sex with him at every opportunity. She probably naively thinks that every Boyfriend is going to be like that, and this is simply not true. She will NEVER regret how much sex she has with her amazing-in-bed boyfriend, but she WILL definitely regret this let's-be-celibate period. (Safe! Safe sex. With condoms. If she's worried about pregnancy and isn't 100% sure condoms will do the job, she can get on the Pill - her mom expressly gives her permission to do so.)<br /><br /><br />ETA: Of course, Bianca has a right to refuse to have sex with Wesley, and make him "work up to it" starting from square one. But her decision really made me upset and uncomfortable. She informs him of this new decision at a crowded bar. She doesn't discuss why she has reached this conclusion. She doesn't talk to him about her feelings or her motivations. They're not even in private! <br /><br />Again, I realize that this is YA and I am analyzing stuff that is not even meant to be analyzed, reading stuff into what is supposed to be a fluffy book. But I can't pretend I'm gung-ho about this sudden, out-of-nowhere, unexplained, major relationship change that she is springing on Wesley. I know he is a "perfect book boyfriend" and just laughs/agrees with everything, but I find what she's doing and the way she's doing it rather distasteful.<br /><br />I can understand her demand for "real dates," i.e. movies, dinners, dances, etc. It's the sex clause I can't wrap my head around.<br /><br />Perhaps Bianca is really confused and uncomfortable with sex? But no, she's not. She seems to be happy and functional in bed. She's also the initiator of 90% of her and Wesley's sexual encounters. If I thought she was emotionally conflicted or had some hang-up about sex or was somehow psychologically unsure about sex in some way, then I would understand what she's doing and be more supportive of her. As it stands, it comes out of left field and makes my head spin.<br /><br />It's absolutely her right to cut him off from sex. And it's absolutely his right to leave her because of that.<br /><br />It's <b>her</b> body but it's <b>their</b> relationship. They need to discuss this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Bad call. I feel like Keplinger is suddenly and for no reason throwing in a don't-have-sex,-teens! message at 98%. It's strange, out-of-place, and unnecessary. As if her publisher or editor was suddenly like, "Well, we can't make it seem like we're promoting teen sex! Whoops! Better just slap a band-aid on that!"<br /><br />FAT<br />The worst, absolute worst parts of the book for me was when Bianca would put herself down by calling herself fat.<br /><br /><i>For a girl with such a fat ass, I felt pretty invisible.</i> AND<br /><br /><i>Casey was bringing popcorn, and Jessica promised us big bowls of chocolate swirl ice cream.<br /><br />As if my ass wasn't big enough.</i> AND<br /><br /><i>...I thought miserably as I lugged my fat ass toward Spanish...</i><br /><br />Listen, the world is going to hate you and tear you down. Why tear yourself down? Why insult yourself? Why be your own bully? I don't understand it. I felt terrible every time Bianca would say something like this. This may be common in female circles, but I can't stand this shit. My friends know better than to disrespect themselves in front of me because they know I will lose my everlovin' mind if I hear them.<br /><br /><br />Tl;dr - This was a mixed bag. On one hand, Bianca is a moron and it is extremely frustrating to the reader. On the other hand, this is a cute, fun, quick read. I enjoyed it overall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15541297649915492984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125586888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16934353456693797712">I'm fully aware of the fact that this does have its flaws but I had such a blast with this book, I can only rate it 5 stars.<br/><br/>Update:<br/><br/>Simply put: I loved this. One reason might be that I’m the biggest sucker on earth for stories like this. Bad boy falls for good/ordinary/average girl. Give me a main character I can relate to, a plot that keeps me entertained and doesn’t strike me as stupid or ridiculous, make the bad boy swoon-worthy and top it off with some hot and sizzling scenes that make my pul</span>
  <span id="freeText16934353456693797712" style="display:none">I'm fully aware of the fact that this does have its flaws but I had such a blast with this book, I can only rate it 5 stars.<br /><br />Update:<br /><br />Simply put: I loved this. One reason might be that I’m the biggest sucker on earth for stories like this. Bad boy falls for good/ordinary/average girl. Give me a main character I can relate to, a plot that keeps me entertained and doesn’t strike me as stupid or ridiculous, make the bad boy swoon-worthy and top it off with some hot and sizzling scenes that make my pulse speed up and I’m happy.<br /><br />As I already said, I am fully aware of the fact that this story does have its flaws, one being its predictability, and you probably wonder why I rated it 5 stars (because this is certainly not the same 5 stars rating as I gave to Melina Marchetta’s Saving Francesca for example) and I honestly don’t know how to justify myself except by saying that I couldn’t put this down, I kept jumping back to passages I especially liked, even while reading, and after I had finished the book I had to read the whole thing again right away because I just didn’t want to let go just yet. Whenever a book manages to cast a spell over me like that I cannot help but give it the highest rating.</span>

<div id="review_2510704001" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2510704001" />
    <a title="Aishu Rehman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73221135-aishu-rehman"><img alt="Aishu Rehman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546532143p2/73221135.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2510704001?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aishu Rehman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aishu Rehman" href="/user/show/73221135-aishu-rehman">Aishu Rehman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444927986" href="/book/show/25076514-the-duff">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2510704001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7374969696533750425">I loved the general idea of this book. As the DUFF in many a friend circles in high school I found this book refreshing. Bianca spends a bit of the book upset by the fact that she is the DUFF, what she learns is that everyone is a DUFF. Which I wish I would’ve known when I was in high school. I loved how it touched on the fact that all teenage girls are so self conscious and never see their true potential. There are a few heavy storylines happening here but in teenage life, they are very common.</span>
  <span id="freeText7374969696533750425" style="display:none">I loved the general idea of this book. As the DUFF in many a friend circles in high school I found this book refreshing. Bianca spends a bit of the book upset by the fact that she is the DUFF, what she learns is that everyone is a DUFF. Which I wish I would’ve known when I was in high school. I loved how it touched on the fact that all teenage girls are so self conscious and never see their true potential. There are a few heavy storylines happening here but in teenage life, they are very common. Bianca’s mom is a motivational speaker and she spends little time at home. It puts a strain on life at the Piper household.<br /><br />Bianca, The Duff, goes out to a teen club with her friends Jessica and Casey. They have fun dancing and she spends most her time chatting up the barkeep named Joe. In comes Wesley Rush. The schools playboy. The boy has a reputation dirtier than yesterdays gym socks. Girls love him because he is your typical teenage heart throb. Muscles, money, and they pretty boy face. He starts chatting with Bianca and tells her all about how she is the Duff and that speaking with her, showing her compassion, will get him high points with her more hot friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7374969696533750425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_108764483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108764483" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108764483?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=swoon-worthy-read">swoon-worthy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108764483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1174017797019936952"><b>My take on Wesley</b> - <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/2011/08/my-book-boyfriend-25-wesley-rush.html'>http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com...</a> (hope you like JJJ :)<br/><br/><b>My Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"No matter where you go or what you do to distract yourself, reality catches up with you eventually".</i><br/><br/>I have never heard of the term The Duff (The Designated Ugly Fat Friend) before I bought this book. I thought maybe it was just a term used in the States. But apparently not. It is even used here in Australia. As I was paying for the book at the counter, the owner of the bookstore said <i>'we used t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1174017797019936952" style="display:none"><b>My take on Wesley</b> - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/2011/08/my-book-boyfriend-25-wesley-rush.html">http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com...</a> (hope you like JJJ :)<br /><br /><b>My Favourite Quote:</b> <i>"No matter where you go or what you do to distract yourself, reality catches up with you eventually".</i><br /><br />I have never heard of the term The Duff (The Designated Ugly Fat Friend) before I bought this book. I thought maybe it was just a term used in the States. But apparently not. It is even used here in Australia. As I was paying for the book at the counter, the owner of the bookstore said <i>'we used to use the same phrase 20 years ago. Every group has a DUFF'.</i> <br /><br />It got me thinking about what role I played in my group. Was I The Duff? But after reading this I realised it is not a bad thing thanks to Keplinger. As Bianca says "<i>I was the Duff. And that was a good thing . Because anyone who didn't feel like the Duff must not have friends. Every girl feels unattractive sometimes.......I should be proud to be the Duff. Proud to have great friends who, in their mind, were my Duffs."</i> That is just one of the reasons why I loved this book.<br /><br />The DUFF is funny, smart, honest, and a heartwarming. It is about all the important issues that all teens deal - love, friendship, family and insecurities. Sounds like an emotional read but it is not really. It had that lighter fun feel to it. A book that you will want to pick up and read again just to feel good. And I am amazed this is Keplinger debut novel and she was only 17 when she wrote it. It is a effortless read that had a nice pace and was always entertaining. <br /><br />Bianca, is instantly likeable character that cause me laughter and heart ache. I think Wesley sums her up perfectly <i>"What you are is an intelligent, sassy, sarcastic, cynical, neurotic, loyal, compassionate girl"</i>. She is confused at times and definitely has some family issues but completely relatable. Bianca doesn't deal with her issues and rather bottles them up inside and looks for other ways to escape them.<br /><br />Now on to my dear Wesley. He makes a great distraction for Bianca. I have to admit at first I disliked him with a passion but as he grew on Bianca, he grew on me too. Definitely a sweetheart (well kind of) hiding as a bad boy. And when you put Bianca and Wes together sparks fly. These two would have to be one of my favourite literary couple because of their witty banter.<br /><br />The only tiny issue I had with this book was the ending. I liked Bianca and Wes' ending that wasn't the problem. But rather the secondary characters - all there issues seemed to be resolved perfectly especially Bianca's Dad and Toby. It was just a tiny bit too perfect because we all know not everybody gets happy endings.<br /><br />Overall, The DUFF is a fantastic debut that you shouldn't miss. <br /><br />Rating: 4.5/5<br /><br />Note: Lots of colourful language and sex scenes. So if you are sensitive to this maybe this book isn't for you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1174017797019936952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1260692938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260692938" />
    <a title="Darth J " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j"><img alt="Darth J " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456429148p2/18974711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260692938?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darth J " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darth J " href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j">Darth J </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260692938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10343692144261466197">In every group there’s a Designated Ugly Fat Friend...<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429888124i/14640533.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And that’s the catchy title and premise of this book, which is predicated on the fact that girl cliques supposedly pick a less attractive girl to hang out with so they can look better by contrast—at least according to our male MC, who the audience is supposed to hate…<br/><br/>I liked a lot of this book because <i>most</i> of it wasn’t typical YA. <i>Most</i> of it didn’t fall into melodrama or unrealistic dialogue. <i>Mostly</i>, this is a <a href='http://24.media.tumblr.com/tumblr_mbu3n2tOvo1qbephpo2_250.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>frank</a> modern tale of the kind of</span>
  <span id="freeText10343692144261466197" style="display:none">In every group there’s a Designated Ugly Fat Friend...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429888124i/14640533.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And that’s the catchy title and premise of this book, which is predicated on the fact that girl cliques supposedly pick a less attractive girl to hang out with so they can look better by contrast—at least according to our male MC, who the audience is supposed to hate…<br><br>I liked a lot of this book because <i>most</i> of it wasn’t typical YA. <i>Most</i> of it didn’t fall into melodrama or unrealistic dialogue. <i>Mostly</i>, this is a <a href="http://24.media.tumblr.com/tumblr_mbu3n2tOvo1qbephpo2_250.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">frank</a> modern tale of the kind of issues teens face today within the high school microcosm.<br><br>Our female MC, Bianca, has her own issues without bringing boy trouble into her life. Her mom is largely absent and her father is a recovering alcoholic. While she has had a crush on another character (with a bowl cut, <i>WTF??</i>) for a few years and has put Vulcan-like barriers of logic in place as to what constitutes love, she can’t help but fall for her hookup buddy <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, who she’s been hate-fucking <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br>I find that this book isn’t so much about the high school experience as an ensemble, but a personal (and all too relatable) tale of being too hard on yourself and not feeling like you’re good enough compared to others. Bianca’s own boundaries are set up to keep people out—while one could argue that this is due to a “broken home”, I find it has more to do with self-esteem issues that most teens face. And <b>that</b> is the real reason why this book caught on and became popular: it’s a universal experience.<br><br>Plus, you just can’t trust anyone who didn’t have awkward teen years. #scientific fact<br><br>This book is also about labels, those we create for ourselves and those we place on others. Slut-shaming occurs here, but surprisingly not only with girls as our male MC gets his fair share of it too from his own grandmother; which is usually just a double-standard. The DUFF is supposedly an insult, but they try to reclaim it to mean something cuter.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429888124i/14640534._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I didn’t like was whom Bianca ends up with. It felt like a complete copout to turn this into a teen fairytale romance towards the end when so much of it held an almost gritty humanity.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10343692144261466197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_248127550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248127550" />
    <a title="Rebekah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah"><img alt="Rebekah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554772145p2/2669249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248127550?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah" href="/user/show/2669249-rebekah">Rebekah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248127550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7084065503500740265">Original Review at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com'>www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I started reading this book all because of the trailer for the movie, it seemed cute and I wanted to read the story. I read it in one sitting, it's a quick read.<br/><br/>So I borrowed the book and read it! Needless to say it's probably going to be nothing like the book but more like the 90's movie <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0160862/?ref_=nv_sr_1' rel='nofollow noopener'>She's All That </a> because this book, was although cute, NOT something I would recommend to young adults.<br/><br/>The main character Bianca was, insecure, self absorbed, </span>
  <span id="freeText7084065503500740265" style="display:none">Original Review at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com">www.awesomebooknuts.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />I started reading this book all because of the trailer for the movie, it seemed cute and I wanted to read the story. I read it in one sitting, it's a quick read.<br /><br />So I borrowed the book and read it! Needless to say it's probably going to be nothing like the book but more like the 90's movie <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0160862/?ref_=nv_sr_1" rel="nofollow noopener">She's All That </a> because this book, was although cute, NOT something I would recommend to young adults.<br /><br />The main character Bianca was, insecure, self absorbed, hypocritical, judgmental, and a bit bitter. Granted I would be upset if I found out I was the DUFF in my group of girlfriends but to do what she did? really?<br /><br />The book is LOADED with sex because Bianca's way of shutting out the world, truth, and her troubles is to have sex with a HOT guy, who has issues of his own, that she absolutely hates because he is everything she hates in a guy and guess what? maybe she didn't realize it but she was just as bad but he was a little less hypocritical about it. GAH! Now, granted everybody has insecurities and I don't mind that but it's hard to read it in a character and what she does with it!<br /><br />How does she even have friends? Am I being a little too hard on her? especially since she is just a fictional character? I think not, especially when it comes to the fact that she finds solace in sex. What is that tell young people? Just have sex when you're upset with the hottest guy who'll have you and maybe it will work out?<br /><br />Well hate to spoil it for you but that is what this book is basically all about. Two people who don't like each other have sex ALL the time and eventually fall for each other. really? dumb...<br /><br />Maybe I didn't understand what the author was saying? because, really, I think I did. Even though the whole thing is about loving yourself and accepting you for who you are, that doesn't justify the content and how the author chose to take this. A bit disappointed here....<br /><br />Overall it could've been super cute and sweet, instead it's not worth your time to read. However I still want to see the movie!<br /><br />Sexual Content: heavy (LOTS of sex-not too graphic and talk of sex)<br />Language: heavy (plenty of all around curse words)<br />Violence: mild (someone getting slapped)<br />Drugs/Alcohol: moderate (underage drinking</span>
  <a data-text-id="7084065503500740265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_123393966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123393966" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123393966?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Someone looking for a silly escape</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4136444-carina">Carina </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123393966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6483401580588418907"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They believed he was a good guy they could tame, but I knew he was a jackass. I only wanted his body.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Go on and get that, girl. <br/><br/>1. At least she KNEW what she was getting herself into.<br/>2. And she owned it without shame.<br/>3. AND she had no expectations that she was going to get more.<br/><br/>In a weird way, Bianca's knowledge of her being the DUFF was this back door into empowerment. In a weird way, I almost expected more insecurity over it. I guess I should be happy that she wasn't the stereotypic</span>
  <span id="freeText6483401580588418907" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>They believed he was a good guy they could tame, but I knew he was a jackass. I only wanted his body.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Go on and get that, girl. <br /><br />1. At least she KNEW what she was getting herself into.<br />2. And she owned it without shame.<br />3. AND she had no expectations that she was going to get more.<br /><br />In a weird way, Bianca's knowledge of her being the DUFF was this back door into empowerment. In a weird way, I almost expected more insecurity over it. I guess I should be happy that she wasn't the stereotypical needy girl who had to have the guy dispelling her insecurities. Using sex to heal wounds can be messy but it's not unrealistic for many people, either. <br /><br />This book was all kinds of backward, which made it that much more enjoyable for me. Yeah, the over-the-top arrogant guy was present front and center, but at least he wasn't being fawned over. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I hated the smooth, confident way he spoke. A lot of girls thought it was sexy, but it was really just stalker-ish. Everything about him screamed date rape! to me. Ugh.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I'M JUST HAPPY to read something where guys aren't fighting over the virginal girl who can't tie her own shoes. Really. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Your sense of humor needs some work, then," Wesley suggested. "Most girls find my jokes charming."<br />"Those girls must have low IQs low enough to trip over."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I could have done without the veiled slut-shaming-turned-lesson-about-how-everyone-is-insecure-so-no-one-should-call-names-ever angle. But whatever. It wasn't that big of a deal. <br /><br /><i>The DUFF</i> was fluffy fun - emphasis on fluff. But don't forget the fun. I like fun. <br /><br />I don't think the movie is going to do the source material justice (they'll probably have to create story content outside of a bedroom, changing the vibe too much), but I'm curious.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6483401580588418907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1689372125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1689372125" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689372125?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316084246" href="/book/show/9662548-the-duff">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689372125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15687851554746092465">Not what I was expecting at all - and not really in a good way.<br/><br/>Now I preface this by saying, to my knowledge, I have never been and have no plans to be a teenage girl. Some of your opinions on my review might be tainted by the fact that I am a middle age man. Well, that's just fine because I am not sure any of what I am about to say is actually applicable. A lot of it will be me being incredulous of the teenage behavior in this book. But, if this is truly how things are, I think I am glad to not</span>
  <span id="freeText15687851554746092465" style="display:none">Not what I was expecting at all - and not really in a good way.<br /><br />Now I preface this by saying, to my knowledge, I have never been and have no plans to be a teenage girl. Some of your opinions on my review might be tainted by the fact that I am a middle age man. Well, that's just fine because I am not sure any of what I am about to say is actually applicable. A lot of it will be me being incredulous of the teenage behavior in this book. But, if this is truly how things are, I think I am glad to not be a teenage girl!<br /><br />I was expecting a coming-of-age, be who you are, it's okay if you are not perfect story. Instead I got a somewhat bitchy and cynical leading lady who was not very endearing and who I wasn't ever really rooting for. She is kinda crummy to her friends and continually blames it on being the unattractive one - even though there really never any descriptions of her as being unattractive unless it is her talking about herself. Even the guy that dubs her the Duff kind of seems to be joking. You might think I am saying she has no self esteem, but it is not really that. It is like she wants to be ugly, uncool, and grumpy.<br /><br />Another criticism is the book is that it is extremely repetitive. She spends most of the time talking about what she isn't going to tell her friends while avoiding them. Some of the things she is hidding really didn't seem to be things best friends could keep from each other while risking breaking up the friendship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i.e. completely avoiding your friends because you are afraid they will find out your dad is drinking again. I understand that may be hard info to share, but she really did almost let it completely destroy her friendship while at the same time sleeping with a hot guy she doesn't want to tell them about either - and then blames it on him. SMH <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Despite my complaints, and concerns that my own daughter's teenage years in a few years, I am giving this 3 stars because I was entertained and the book did have me engaged by having me driven to curse at Bianca every few pages, so that must count for something!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15687851554746092465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X2e+RNTNF277lroZOm6OX7l6xwNTNYKrWGyEJCMgEd4Cgq50NMNc2NO6XtVBM6ScAbfvtbl6hSPGwk83BM4LWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DefROBjwc7DbR/wgez7vea3uY4WrusCW7GN1tGVBcZ5QAsEI+P44BvNrGOwAY8W6FSNLM0H1xx5yzb6nQq9rGw==')})
  }
